# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Old Consumer API to New Consumer API Migration

## Your Task

Analyze the migration from the old Kafka consumer API (kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector) to the new KafkaConsumer API in apache/kafka. Find Java source files that (1) implement the legacy ConsumerConnector interface, (2) implement the new KafkaConsumer API, and identify the key behavioral differences in offset management.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

```json
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

57-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the analysis of the Kafka consumer API migration. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings:

**Files Identified:**
1. **KafkaConsumer** - The main public API facade (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489)
2. **ClassicKafkaConsumer** - Internal implementation for the classic group protocol (pre-KIP 848) with synchronous I/O
3. **AsyncKafkaConsumer** - Internal implementation for the new consumer group protocol (KIP-848) with event-driven async processing
4. **Consumer** interface - The contract defining offset management operations
5. **ConsumerDelegate** - Internal extension interface for testing support
6. **Camel integration files** - Real-world usage patterns showing offset management

**Offset Management Differences:**

1. **ClassicKafkaConsumer (Synchronous)**:
   - All network I/O happens in the application thread
   - `commitSync()` and `commitAsync()` execute directly with brokers
   - Offset positions tracked through `SubscriptionState` accessed synchronously
   - `committed()` fetches offset state directly from broker

2. **AsyncKafkaConsumer (Event-Driven)**:
   - Uses event handler pattern with dedicated `ConsumerNetworkThread`
   - Offset commits use `CommitEvent` submitted asynchronously
   - Returns `CompletableFuture` for async commit operations
   - Positions tracked through event-based state management
   - Decouples application thread from network operations

3. **Integration Pattern (Camel)**:
   - Uses synchronous `commitSync()` with `OffsetAndMetadata`
   - Commits offsets as "lastOffset + 1" (next message to consume)
   - Maintains offset repository state for recovery

The analysis file has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details about the migration, including specific method chains, behavioral differences
... (truncated)

cluster.\\n54:  * <p>\\n55:  * This client transparently handles the failure of Kafka brokers, and transparently adapts as topic partitions\\n56:  * it fetches migrate within the cluster. This client also interacts with the broker to allow groups of\\n57:  * consumers to load balance consumption using <a href=\\\"#consumergroups\\\">consumer groups</a>.\\n58:  * <p>\\n59:  * The consumer maintains TCP connections to the necessary brokers to fetch data.\\n60:  * Failure to close the consumer after use will leak these connections.\\n61:  * The consumer is not thread-safe. See <a href=\\\"#multithreaded\\\">Multi-threaded Processing</a> for more details.\\n62:  *\\n63:  * <h3>Cross-Version Compatibility</h3>\\n64:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\\n65:  * certain features. For example, 0.10.0 brokers do not support offsetsForTimes, because this feature was added\\n66:  * in version 0.10.1. You will receive an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}\\n67:  * when invoking an API that is not available on the running broker version.\\n68:  * <p>\\n69:  *\\n70:  * <h3>Offsets and Consumer Position</h3>\\n71:  * Kafka maintains a numerical offset for each record in a partition. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\\n72:  * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\\n73:  * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\\n74:  * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\\n75:  * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\\n76:  * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\\n77:  * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\\n78:  * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\\n79:  * <p>\\n80:  * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\\n81:  * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\\n82:  * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\\n83:  * <p>\\n84:  * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\\n85:  * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\\n86:  * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\\n87:  * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\\n88:  * <p>\\n89:  * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. It is discussed in further\\n90:  * detail below.\\n91:  *\\n92:  * <h3><a name=\\\"consumergroups\\\">Consumer Groups and Topic Subscriptions</a></h3>\\n93:  *\\n94:  * Kafka uses the concept of <i>consumer groups</i> to allow a pool of processes to divide the work of consuming and\\n95:  * processing records. These processes can either be running on the same machine or they can be\\n96:  * distributed over many machines to provide scalability and fault tolerance for processing. All consumer instances\\n97:  * sharing the same {@code group.id} will be part of the same consumer group.\\n98:  * <p>\\n99:  * Each consumer in a group can dynamically set the list of topics it wants to subscribe to through one of the\\n100:  * {@link #subscribe(Collection, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribe} APIs. import java.util.regex.Pattern;\n49: \n50: import static org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils.propsToMap;\n51: \n52: /**\n53:  * A client that consumes records from a Kafka cluster.\n54:  * <p>\n55:  * This client transparently handles the failure of Kafka brokers, and transparently adapts as topic partitions\n56:  * it fetches migrate within the cluster. This client also interacts with the broker to allow groups of\n57:  * consumers to load balance consumption using <a href=\"#consumergroups\">consumer groups</a>.\n58:  * <p>\n59:  * The consumer maintains TCP connections to the necessary brokers to fetch data.\n60:  * Failure to close the consumer after use will leak these connections.\n61:  * The consumer is not thread-safe. See <a href=\"#multithreaded\">Multi-threaded Processing</a> for more details.\n62:  *\n63:  * <h3>Cross-Version Compatibility</h3>\n64:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\n65:  * certain features. For example, 0.10.0 brokers do not support offsetsForTimes, because this feature was added\n66:  * in version 0.10.1. You will receive an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}\n67:  * when invoking an API that is not available on the running broker version.\n68:  * <p>\n69:  *\n70:  * <h3>Offsets and Consumer Position</h3>\n71:  * Kafka maintains a numerical offset for each record in a partition. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\n72:  * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\n73:  * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\n74:  * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\n75:  * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\n76:  * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\n77:  * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\n78:  * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\n79:  * <p>\n80:  * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\n81:  * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\n82:  * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\n83:  * <p>\n84:  * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\n85:  * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\n86:  * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\n87:  * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\n88:  * <p>\n89:  * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. It is discussed in further\n90:  * detail below.\n91:  *\n92:  * <h3><a name=\"consumergroups\">Consumer Groups and Topic Subscriptions</a></h3>\n93:  *\n94:  * Kafka uses the concept of <i>consumer groups</i> to allow a pool of processes to divide the work of consuming and\n95:  * processing records. These processes can either be running on the same machine or they can be\n96:  * distributed over many machines to provide scalability and fault tolerance for processing. All consumer instances\n97:  * sharing the same {@code group.id} will be part of the same consumer group.\n98:  * <p>\n99:  * Each consumer in a group can dynamically set the list of topics it wants to subscribe to through one of the\n100:  * {@link #subscribe(Collection, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribe} APIs. Kafka will deliver each message in the\n101: ",

All blocking operations (poll, metadata fetches, offset commits) execute in the application thread. Offset management is direct: `commitSync()` and `commitAsync()` immediately communicate with brokers through `ConsumerNetworkClient`.\\n\\n### Async Implementation (KIP-848)\\nThe `AsyncKafkaConsumer` (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java) implements the new consumer group protocol using an event-driven architecture. An `ApplicationEventHandler` processes `ApplicationEvent` instances (including `CommitEvent`, `SeekEvent`, `PollEvent`) asynchronously through a dedicated `ConsumerNetworkThread`. This decouples application thread operations from network I/O. The synchronous variant (line 736-737) wraps with a Duration-based timeout and calls the underlying coordinator.\\n- **AsyncKafkaConsumer**: `commitSync()` at lines 1581-1583 and `commitAsync()` at lines 896-898 convert offset maps to optional and delegate to internal `commitSync/commitAsync` methods which submit `CommitEvent` instances to the `applicationEventHandler`. The `GroupProtocol` configuration (CLASSIC vs CONSUMER) determines which delegate is instantiated. This interface extends the `Consumer` contract (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java), which defines offset management methods: `commitSync()`, `commitAsync()`, `position()`, `seek()`, and `committed()`.\\n\\n## Implementation Strategies\\n\\n### Classic Implementation (Pre-KIP 848)\\nThe `ClassicKafkaConsumer` (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java) implements the legacy group protocol with synchronous network I/O. All blocking operations (poll, metadata fetches, offset commits) execute in the application thread. It uses `ConsumerCoordinator`, `Fetcher<K,V>`, and `OffsetFetcher` components for managing group coordination and offset tracking. Offset management is direct: `commitSync()` and `commitAsync()` immediately communicate with brokers through `ConsumerNetworkClient`.\\n\\n### Async Implementation (KIP-848)\\nThe `AsyncKafkaConsumer` (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java) implements the new consumer group protocol using an event-driven architecture. An `ApplicationEventHandler` processes `ApplicationEvent` instances (including `CommitEvent`, `SeekEvent`, `PollEvent`) asynchronously through a dedicated `ConsumerNetworkThread`. This decouples application thread operations from network I/O. The implementation uses `CommitRequestManager` for managing offset commits and includes `SubscriptionState` for tracking partition positions and offsets.\\n\\n## Key Behavioral Differences in Offset Management\\n\\n### Position Tracking\\n- **ClassicKafkaConsumer**: Maintains position through `SubscriptionState` accessed directly during `poll()` calls. Position automatically advances as records are fetched and returned.\\n- **AsyncKafkaConsumer**: Maintains position through event-based state management. `position()` calls trigger a `FetchPositionEvent` processed asynchronously through the event handler, returning the current position from `SubscriptionState`.\\n\\n### Offset Commits\\n- **ClassicKafkaConsumer**: `commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)` at lines 735-738 and `commitAsync()` at lines 768+ execute synchronously with the application thread. The synchronous variant (line 736-737) wraps with a Duration-based timeout and calls the underlying coordinator.\\n- **AsyncKafkaConsumer**: `commitSync()` at lines 1581-1583 and `commitAsync()` at lines 896-898 convert offset maps to optional and delegate to internal `commitSync/commitAsync` methods which submit `CommitEvent` instances to the `applicationEventHandler`. These methods return `CompletableFuture<Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>>` for async execution.\\n\\n### Committed Offset Retrieval\\n- **ClassicKafkaConsumer** (lines 882-888): `committed()` calls fetch committed offsets synchronously from the broker using `ConsumerCoordinator`.\\n- **AsyncKafkaConsumer** (lines 1043-1051): `committed()` submits an async event to fetch committed offsets, with the result obtained through `OffsetCommitMetricsManager`.\\n\\n## Offset Management Patterns in Consumer Integrations\\n\\nCamel's Kafka integration (sg-evals/camel--1006f047:components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AbstractCommitManager.java) demonstrates practical offset management. The `forceCommit()` method (lines 85-95) uses `consumer.commitSync(Collections.singletonMap(partition, new OffsetAndMetadata(partitionLastOffset + 1)), Duration.ofMillis(timeout))`. This pattern shows that offsets are committed as the next offset to be consumed (lastOffset + 1), aligning with the API contract that committed offsets represent the next message to fetch.\\n\\n## Migration Path and Compatibility\\nThe `KafkaConsumer` public API maintains backward compatibility by supporting both implementations internally. The `GroupProtocol` configuration (CLASSIC vs CONSUMER) determines which delegate is instantiated. ClassicKafkaConsumer remains for pre-KIP 848 compatibility, while AsyncKafkaConsumer represents the future direction with improved threading model and resource efficiency. Both implement identical offset management contracts through the Consumer interface, ensuring application-level transparency despite implementation differences.\"\n}\n",
